=== SEARCH SNIPPETS ===

[1972 Canadian federal budget - Wikipedia]
The 1972 Canadian federal budget for fiscal year 1972-73 was presented by Minister of Finance John N. Turner in the House of Commons of Canada on 8 May 1972. It was the last budget before the 1972 Canadian federal election, and included tax cuts for corporations, and aid for the elderly and post-secondary students.
URL: https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1972_Canadian_federal_budget

[PDF GOVERNMENT ORDERS - lop.parl.ca]
Under the present rules, taxpayers could base their instalment payments either on their esti- mate of the current year's liability or, alternatively, on a computation involving the prior year's income and the current year's tax rates.
URL: https://lop.parl.ca/staticfiles/ParlInfo/Documents/Budgets/En/1972-05-08.pdf

[High‐Spending Ottawa Budget To Create Jobs Is Announced]
May 9, 1972 · The budget, presented to the House of Commons, envisions expenditures in the fiscal year that began April 1 totaling $16.1‐billion, compared with $14.7‐billion In 1971–1972.
URL: https://www.nytimes.com/1972/05/09/archives/highspending-ottawa-budget-to-create-jobs-is-announced.html

[PDF Res A29a 1972 IS Finance Finances - epe.lac-bac.gc.ca]
Mr. Speaker: My first words to this House as Minister of Finance last February were that my most urgent priority was jobs. This remains my first priority. No economy is working as well as it should if there are men and women seeking work who cannot find it. The search for jobs is a human problem. The main thrust of this budget is to deal with this problem; to buttress the Canadian economy - to ...
URL: https://epe.lac-bac.gc.ca/100/201/301/budget-e/2014/www.budget.gc.ca/pdfarch/1972-sd-eng.pdf?nodisclaimer=1

[PDF Budget Highlights 1972 - publications.gc.ca]
In the 1971-72 fiscal year ended March 31, 1972, budgetary revenues are estimated at $14,145 million and expenditures at $14,745 million, for a $600 million deficit.
URL: https://publications.gc.ca/collections/collection_2016/fin/F12-10-1972-eng.pdf

--- [High‐Spending Ottawa Budget To Create Jobs Is Announced] ---
Supported by High‐Spending Ottawa Budget To Create Jobs Is Announced May 9, 1972, Page 6Buy Reprints OTTAWA, May 8—The Government tonight announced record‐high expenditures for the coming year to create jobs in what it called a strong but changing economy. The budget, presented to the House of Commons, envisions expenditures in the fiscal year that began April 1 totaling $16.1‐billion, compared with $14.7‐billion In 1971–1972. It requires the approval of Parliament. The budget calls for “incentive” tax cuts for Canadian manufacturers, including the more than 50 per cent that are owned or controlled by United States investors. It also proposes broadened “earned depletion” incentives to encourage expanded ore mining operations. “Jobs remained first priority,” Finance Minister John N. Turner told Parliament. But he insisted that Canada's 6 per cent rate of unemployment was the result of an erratic increase in the labor force. New Jobs Created “Twice as many new jobs were created in Canada last year as in 1970,” Mr. Turner said, “but because of rapid labor force growth the decline in unemployment began only in the latter part of the year.” The budget also calls for substantial increases in old‐age and veterans pensions and allowances and increases in tax exemptions for persons who have reached 65 years to $1,000 from $650. There would also be special tax exemtpions of $50 a month for full‐time trainees and students taking post‐high school training courses, The benefit increases were estimated to cost $425‐million. Mr. Turner's budget speech made no mention of the elections that Prime Minister Pierre Elliott Trudeau is expected to call next summer or fall. But opposition leaders, who will open debate on the budget, hinted privately tonight they will attack it as an “election budget.” Unemployment Attacked Robert L. Stanfield, the Conservative leader and David Lewis, leader of the left‐wing New Democrats, have made high unemployment the focus of their attack on Mr. Trudeau's Government. Public ‐ opinion polls have shown the Government Liberals slumping in popularity because so many Canadians are out of jobs. To provide incentives for Canadian industry, Mr. Turner announced that, under the proposed budget, the general corporate tax rate on Canadian manufacturers would be reduced to 40 per cent from an average of 50 per cent, effective Jan. 1, 1973. “The only realistic solution for matching the tremendous yearly increase in our work force is greater growth in the economy,” said Mr. Turner. “It is growth that will create jobs. We have to look to expansion of Canadian industry to provide those jobs.” Tax cuts would be partly offset by the expected growth in the economy‐6 to 6.5 per cent, in the Finance Minister's estimate. But the revenues will run behind expenditures by about $450‐million, Mr. Turner said. This year's deficit was $600 million. Related Content Advertisement
